### Question 2: Can you differentiate a cross-listed course and elective applied course in the case of a double major?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can differentiate a cross-listed course and an elective applied course in the case of a double major.

Cross-listed courses are shared between two majors or a major and a minor, and they can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements up to a maximum of 8 credits (two courses) per pair of majors or major and minor. This limit applies per pair and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim.

Elective applied courses, on the other hand, are courses from other majors that emphasize the applications of Mathematics. Students must take at least 2 applied courses (at least one at the 200 level), and if there are any prerequisites, students need to either complete the course's prerequisites or obtain the instructor's approval. These courses do not have a specific credit limit for double majors.

Additionally, students may not double count a course for two different requirements. For example, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced Course or 1 Elective Applied Course, but not both. Therefore, it is important to carefully plan and consult with an academic advisor to ensure that courses are used appropriately to meet the requirements of both majors.  

<details>

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. ### Question 3: I would like to ask for the capstone withdrawal policy. What will be the impact when I choose to drop the capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts? Will there be any penalties associated with withdrawing, such as a 'W' notation on my transcript?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided context, if you withdraw from the Capstone course before the Fall 2025 term starts, you will not receive a 'W' notation on your transcript, as the withdrawal occurs outside of the specified term periods mentioned in the document. The policy states that for a withdrawal request submitted from Week 3 to Week 4 of the term, there are no consequences in the Academic Records. Since the Capstone course is not part of a specific term but rather a standalone course, and given that you are asking about its withdrawal before the term starts, it falls under the category where no 'W' grade or other academic record notations will be made. Therefore, there should be no penalties associated with withdrawing from the Capstone course prior to the start of the Fall 2025 term. However, it's always advisable to consult with your Academic/Major Advisor to ensure compliance with all university policies and procedures.

WITHDRAWAL FROM THE UNIVERSITY: All students who decide to end their education at Fulbright, or who apply for but do not qualify for a leave of absence and still take leave, or who wish to transfer to another institution are expected to formally withdraw from the University. Normally a student cannot stay on campus upon withdrawal. For extenuating circumstances that require a student to stay on campus past their withdrawal date, the student must apply for permission from the Vice President of Student Affairs. A student who is placed on Administrative Leave of Absence status for one term without formally withdrawing or receiving approval for a leave extension before the term census date (Friday of Week 4) will be considered as having withdrawn without permission and may be administratively withdrawn.

### Question 4: Questions related to course history, in which one course can have multiple IDs? Like Advanced Deep Learning course. How would it be handled among different cohorts?  
### Answer: 

When a course like Advanced Deep Learning has multiple IDs and is offered to different cohorts, it typically means that the course content may evolve over time or be tailored slightly for each cohort. Here's how it could be handled:

1. **Course Versioning**: Each ID could represent a different version of the course. For example, ID 1 might refer to the original version, while ID 2 could indicate an updated or revised version with new materials, assignments, or teaching methods.

2. **Cohort-Specific Content**: Different IDs could correspond to different cohorts, where each cohort receives a unique set of materials, assignments, or projects tailored to their specific needs or learning styles. This ensures that each group gets the most relevant and beneficial experience.

3. **Tracking Progress**: The institution might maintain a record of which ID corresponds to which cohort, allowing them to track progress, performance, and feedback more effectively.

4. **Flexibility in Curriculum**: If the course content changes significantly between versions, the institution might decide to reassign students to a new ID if they are starting a new cohort, ensuring they receive the latest and most relevant information.

5. **Consistency Across Cohorts**: In some cases, the institution might choose to offer the same course content across all IDs, ensuring consistency in learning outcomes despite the different IDs.

Ultimately, the handling of multiple IDs for the same course depends on the institution's policies and goals, but the key is maintaining clear communication about which ID corresponds to which cohort and what the expectations are for each.

### Question 5: I have taken Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis in Fall 2023. Am I eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you are eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024. According to the information provided, Advanced level courses in Economics can be taken after completing at least one of Microeconomic and Macroeconomic Analysis and Econometrics. Since you have already completed Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis, you meet the prerequisite for taking Financial Economics. However, please ensure that you also meet any other prerequisites or requirements specified for the Financial Economics course. It's advisable to consult with an advisor to confirm your eligibility and plan your course schedule accordingly.

### Question 6: If I have waived the course Computer Science I, but I want to declare Computer Science major, do I have to take Computer Science I?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you have to take Computer Science I if you want to declare Computer Science as your major. Waiving the course does not exempt you from the requirement to complete it as part of the major. According to the provided information, "To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses (MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted)." Since Computer Science I is a required course for the major, you would need to take it unless there's an alternative approved by the department. However, waiving a course typically means you've already completed its equivalent, so you might need to discuss this with your academic advisor to ensure you meet all the requirements.

Courses in Computer Science go beyond content to help students learn through direct experiences in projects and problems. Students will also have the opportunity to further focus their studies by selecting a concentration, such as software engineering, artificial intelligence and machine learning, data science, business analytics. ### Question 7: If I have taken the following courses: Mathematical Statistics, Abstract Algebra, Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, Calculus, Differential Equation, Stochastic Calculus, Statistical Learning, Discrete Mathematics, Probability, am I eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics? What about majoring in Applied Mathematics?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you have taken several courses that align with the requirements for both a minor and a major in Applied Mathematics.

For a minor in Applied Mathematics:
- You have taken Linear Algebra, Calculus, and Introduction to Statistics (Mathematical Statistics).
- You have taken at least one Pure Mathematics course (Abstract Algebra).
- You have taken at least two advanced courses (Stochastic Calculus and Statistical Learning).

You have also taken additional courses like Multivariable Calculus, Differential Equation, and Discrete Mathematics, which could count towards electives or other requirements.

For a major in Applied Mathematics:
- You have taken Linear Algebra, Calculus, and Introduction to Statistics (Mathematical Statistics).
- You have taken at least one Pure Mathematics course (Abstract Algebra).
- You have taken at least two advanced courses (Stochastic Calculus and Statistical Learning).
- You have taken at least two Elective Applied courses (Discrete Mathematics and Probability).

Given your coursework, you meet the requirements for both a minor and a major in Applied Mathematics. However, since you have already taken more than the minimum required courses for a minor, you might want to consult with an academic advisor to determine the best path forward. They can help you decide whether to pursue a minor or a major, considering your interests and career goals. 

Remember, the exact eligibility may depend on specific university policies and the current curriculum. It's always a good idea to confirm with your academic advisor.

### Question 13: If I major in Economics, is it sufficient that I take Scholar Development to fulfill Experiential Learning requirements?  
### Answer: 

No, taking Scholar Development alone is not sufficient to fulfill the Experiential Learning requirements for an Economics major. According to the provided context, students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. The specific courses or programs that count towards this requirement are not detailed in the given information, but it is clear that Scholar Development alone does not meet the ELP criteria. Therefore, additional courses or experiences within the ELP framework would be necessary to fulfill this requirement.

### Question 14: Is it sufficient for me to complete 4 credits in EL if I major in Engineering?  
### Answer: 

No, it is not sufficient to complete only 4 credits in Experiential Learning (EL) if you major in Engineering. According to the provided information, students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. Therefore, completing exactly 4 credits would meet the minimum requirement but does not account for the possibility of exceeding this minimum and fulfilling the maximum requirement of 12 credits. Additionally, the context suggests that experiential learning can count towards elective or major requirements with advisor approval, so completing 4 credits might be part of a broader fulfillment strategy. However, simply completing 4 credits alone does not fully satisfy the Experiential Learning requirement for an Engineering major.

For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. ### Question 15: Can I take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses. Typically, students are required to take six 200-level intermediate courses and four 300-level advanced courses. The provided context suggests that until a robust list of 200 and 300-Level Courses is available, students can satisfy the 48 Credits with any combination of 200 and 300 Level Courses, but it also emphasizes the importance of adhering to the above requirements when selecting courses where possible. Therefore, taking only two intermediate engineering courses would not meet the typical requirement. It's advisable to follow the recommended course structure to ensure you meet the necessary credit requirements.

### Question 16: If I have completed the course Intro to AI, will CS207 - Object-Oriented Analysis and Design and CS211 – Operating Systems suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses?  
### Answer: 

No, CS207 and CS211 alone will not suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses. According to the provided information, the minor requires students to take a total of six courses, including one intermediate course. Therefore, you would need to select two more intermediate courses from the available options to fulfill the requirement. Courses like CS203: Computer Organization or any other intermediate-level CS courses could be considered for this purpose. CS207 and CS211 are advanced courses, not intermediate ones, so they cannot be used to satisfy the intermediate course requirement.

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 19]
networks and systems. CS201: Data Structures & Algorithms Prerequisites: CS101 How do we write large programs to solve real-world problems correctly and eﬀiciently? How do we design programs that can be tested and extended easily? This course aims to achieve these goals by expanding the content from CS101 (Introduction to Programming), with a greater focus on theoretical concepts, abstraction, and larger programs. Topics include object-oriented programming (classes, objects, subclasses, and inheritances), unit testing and refactoring, fundamental data structures (arrays, lists, stacks, queues, trees, hash tables, and graphs), basic algorithms (sorting and searching) and their analysis. Java is the main programming language used in the course but some Python/C++ implementations are also introduced. CS203: Computer Organization Prerequisites: CORE105– Design & Systems Thinking Computing systems, such as mobile phones, laptops or personal computers, have been an important parts of human beings’ everyday life.

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 19]
(AI) is a research ﬁeld that studies how to realize the intelligent human behaviors on a computer. The ultimate goal of AI is to make a computer that can learn, plan, and solve problems autonomously. In this course, student will learn the foundational principles and practice implementing some of these applications including representation, problem solving, and learning methods of artiﬁcial intelligence. Accordingly, students should be able to develop intelligent systems by assembling solutions to concrete computational problems; understand the role of knowledge representation, problem solving, and learning in intelligent-system engineering; and appreciate the role of problem solving, vision, and language in understanding human intelligence from a computational perspective. ### Question 17: Does completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfy the core theory requirement, or is an additional course needed?  
### Answer: 

Completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfies the core theory requirement. An additional course is not needed according to the provided information.

### Question 18: If I want to major in Engineering, can I choose other programming courses besides Computer Science I and Computer Science II, for instance Introduction to data visualization?  
### Answer: 

No, for a major in Computer Science, you cannot choose other programming courses besides Computer Science I and Computer Science II, or Introduction to Data Visualization. The provided information specifies that for a Computer Science major, you must take either CS 101: Introduction to Programming, CS 103: Programming for Data Science and Visualization, or CS 104: Introduction to Computer Science as your programming course. Since you're asking about majoring in Engineering, it's likely that the specific requirements for Engineering would differ, but the given context pertains specifically to Computer Science major requirements. Therefore, for an Engineering major, you would need to check the specific programming courses required for that major. Based on the information provided, Introduction to Data Visualization does not appear to be one of the specified options for a Computer Science major. Thus, for a Computer Science major, you cannot choose Introduction to Data Visualization as your programming course. For Engineering majors, please refer to the specific Engineering program requirements.

### Question 19: Given I took Discrete Mathematics in Spring 2022 and earned B, then the same course in Spring 2024 and earned C-, which grades will be kept?  
### Answer: 

The higher grade, which is the B from Spring 2022, will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade, which is the C- from Spring 2024, will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and will remain on the transcript.

### Question 20: Can I register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4. According to the context provided, exploratory courses E4-Mathematics and Computing are limited to courses at the 100-level or 200-level. Courses at the 300-level do not qualify for this category. Therefore, only 100-level or 200-level math courses can be considered for fulfilling the E4 requirement. Any 300-level math courses would need to be registered under a different category if they are part of your major or elective requirements.

### Question 21: Can I register for more than 20 credits in a semester?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register for more than 20 credits in a semester according to the information provided in the given text. The form mentioned in the context is specifically for requesting the registration of the maximum course load of 20 credit hours per term. Therefore, it implies that the standard course load is less than 20 credits, and exceeding this limit requires a specific request and approval process. Hence, registering for more than 20 credits would not be allowed without completing and submitting the appropriate form and obtaining the Academic Advisor's approval.

### Question 22: What is the maximum number of times I can retake a course to improve my grade, and how does it affect my transcript?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided information, a student may retake the same course up to three times. Here's how it affects the transcript:

1. If a student receives a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP' for the course, or withdraws and receives a grade of 'W', they are required to repeat the course.
2. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after receiving a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with the student's academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. This includes course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year.
3. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation.
4. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript.
5. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits.
6. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements.
7. Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.

### Question 23: For a student doing the literature capstone, if a student includes charts or tables, do they count toward the word limit?  
### Answer: 

Charts or tables do not count toward the word limit for the literature capstone. According to the guidelines provided, the word count should be between 6,000 and 10,000 words, excluding full bibliography and images with captions. Therefore, while charts and tables are part of the overall content, they do not contribute to the word count. However, it's important to note that the specific formatting and citation style should follow the Chicago Style, 17th Edition.

### Question 25: If I do Literature capstone in Decolonial studies, can it be approved?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided information, whether a capstone project in Decolonial studies within the Literature program can be approved depends on several factors:

1. **Eligibility Criteria**: You need to have a Major GPA of 3.5 by the beginning of Capstone I and no outstanding Incompletes at the time of application.
2. **Proposal Quality**: Your proposal will be assessed by the major faculty based on its quality.
3. **Advising Process**: You will be matched to your first or second choice of advisors, depending on availability.

Decolonial studies can certainly align with the Literature capstone's objectives, especially given the Literature Program Learning Outcomes, particularly MLO5 which focuses on comparing historical and transnational literary traditions with attention to social, political, and conceptual nuances. However, the specific focus on Decolonial studies would need to fit within the broader framework of the Literature major and meet the eligibility criteria mentioned above.

Therefore, if your proposal demonstrates how Decolonial studies fits into the Literature major and meets the required GPA and other criteria, it could potentially be approved. It is advisable to discuss your idea with the major capstone coordinator or your potential advisors to ensure it aligns with the program's expectations.

[Source: Literature Capstone Handbook.pdf, Page: 8]
1. General Information: The Literature Capstone is a culmination of a student’s curriculum through an individual project involving independent research. Through support from existing faculty, students propose, undertake, and write up a research or creative writing project over the course of two consecutive semesters, labelled as Capstone I and Capstone II. Students are encouraged to conduct primary and secondary research, even for creative projects. Fieldwork, however, is not expected at this level. Students are also expected to think very carefully about an appropriate scope of research and production plan for the proposed capstone. The project may also draw from academic coursework, relevant extracurricular activities or practical experience to support the research and realization of the project. At the end of the year, students present their work in a symposium for peers and the greater Fulbright community. ### Question 27: Can Discrete Mathematics be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors?  
### Answer: 

Yes, Discrete Mathematics (MATH 202) can be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors. This course is part of the requirements for both majors, demonstrating its relevance and applicability across these disciplines.

### Question 28: What steps should I take to ensure a smooth transfer of my exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

To ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright, you should follow these steps:

1. Gather all necessary information: Collect detailed information about the courses you took during your exchange semester at Bard College. This includes the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

2. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer: Fill out the Application for Credit Transfer form provided by Fulbright. Make sure to attach your official transcript from Bard College.

3. Provide required information: Along with the application, provide all the requested information about the courses you want to transfer. This ensures that Fulbright can evaluate your courses accurately.

4. Submit the application: Send the completed application and supporting documents to the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright University Vietnam.

5. Consult with your Academic Advisor: It's important to discuss your program plan with your Academic Advisor to ensure that the transferred credits align with your degree requirements.

6. Await evaluation: The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether the credit transfer is justified according to Fulbright's policies.

7. Follow up: Keep track of the status of your application and be prepared to provide additional information if needed.

By following these steps, you can facilitate a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright. Remember to stay organized and proactive throughout the process.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. ### Question 29: Are 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement?  
### Answer: 

Yes, 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 are also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. The context specifies that students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. This implies that only courses explicitly categorized in these three categories can be used to fulfill the Exploratory requirements. Courses not categorized in these areas do not count towards the Exploratory requirement.

### Question 31: If I withdraw from a course after the 4th week of the semester, will I be deducted 4 credits of financial aid?  
### Answer: 

No, you will not be deducted 4 credits of financial aid if you withdraw from a course after the 4th week of the semester. The context states that no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, the financial aid is not directly affected by the number of credits you are left with after withdrawal. However, maintaining a minimum of 12 credits per term is required to maintain full-time enrollment status. If you fall below this threshold due to withdrawals, you might face other implications such as loss of financial aid eligibility or other academic standing issues.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. Exceptions will only be permitted in exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.  Students should be aware that course withdrawals may

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 25]
[F03 – RO/FUV]: Course Withdrawal Request From Week 3 to Week 4 of the term, a student can request to withdraw the course(s) without any consequences in the Academic Records. From Week 5 to Week 8 of the term, attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript which does not affect the student’s GPA. Please consult with your Academic/Major Advisor before withdrawing from the course. Refer to the Fees and Charges Guide for further information about fees related to the withdrawal weeks. ### Question 32: Why do I need to take 8 exploratory courses?  
### Answer: 

You need to take 8 exploratory courses to step out of your comfort zone and explore broad areas of study, helping you discover more fully where your interests and passions lie. This requirement aims to broaden your academic experience and ensure you gain knowledge across different disciplines.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 12]
and discover more fully where their interests and passions lie. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulﬁll more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. ### Question 33: Can I take 160 credits in 4 years given that I pay for the full tuition fee?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you cannot take 160 credits in 4 years because the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. Therefore, even if you pay for the full tuition fee, you are limited by the maximum time frame for completing the program. Typically, a full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term, and students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Given these constraints, it is not possible to accumulate 160 credits in 4 years.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours.  The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or

A student wishing to do a capstone must apply during the term prior to the first term of the capstone (Capstone I), and may only apply after having completed 80 credits of coursework. ### Question 34: What are the requirements for mathematics courses to pursue Human-Centered Engineering major?  
### Answer: 

To pursue the Human-Centered Engineering major while focusing on Mathematics, students must meet the following requirements:

1. **Take at least 2 advanced courses** in areas such as:
   - Applied Statistics (e.g., Economics, Social Sciences, Mathematical Finance, Bioinformatics)
   - Engineering Mathematics (e.g., Signal processing, Numerical simulation, Inverse problems)
   - Data Science (e.g., Machine learning, Artificial intelligence)

2. **Consultation with an academic advisor** is required for course selection.

These advanced courses aim to deepen students' understanding of how mathematical principles can be applied to solve real-world engineering problems, aligning with the human-centered approach of the major. Additionally, students should ensure that they meet the prerequisites for these advanced courses or obtain the instructor's approval if needed. This pathway complements the broader curriculum by integrating mathematical expertise with engineering applications.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 46]
HUMAN-CENTERED ENGINEERING: (Starting from academic year 2022-2023) Description The term "Engineer", as per the Encyclopedia Britannica, finds its etymological roots in the Latin word "Engine," denoting creation. Engineers are esteemed individuals dedicated to the innovation and development of devices, products, and machinery aimed at benefiting humanity. Engineering, meanwhile, embodies the systematic application of scientific principles to transform raw natural resources into refined end products. Centuries have passed since that first definition, and Engineers still stay true to the mission of serving human kind. Technologies and methodologies are, however, so much different now. Artificial Intelligence (AI) is now avaible to the public and being utilized to create new content, from text to image to motion picture. In the coming years, the rapid growth of AI is anticipated to persist, enabling its application in solving adaptive problems. This foreseeable landscape will bring in many new opportunities for

### Question 35: How is the grade of a replaced course displayed on the transcript? Will it replace the old one or create a new entry in the transcript?  
### Answer: 

The grade of a replaced course is displayed on the transcript by overwriting the old grade with the notation "RP", meaning "repeated". This notation remains on the transcript alongside the higher grade, which is kept and used in the GPA calculation. Therefore, the replaced course does not create a new entry but rather updates the existing record.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. ### Question 36: What are the courses that can replace the capstone for a given major?  
### Answer: 

For the Economics major, students who do not intend to complete a Capstone project must complete an additional two Advanced level courses instead of the Capstone. There is no information provided regarding other majors and their respective alternatives to the capstone.

1. What is a capstone in Computer Science?: According to university-wide policy, the capstone is a culmination to the student’s curriculum to demonstrates the principal learning outcomes and competencies of that curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way. In the Computer Science major, the capstone is an individual project and can take only the form of a written thesis. The capstone should demonstrate original critical and creative thinking, and we encourage primary research. You should think very carefully about an appropriate scope of research and production for your proposed capstone. Keep in mind that projects for which there is no current faculty expertise may not be approved. It is important for you to consult early on with your potential advisor to ensure the matchs. Applications which do not demonstrate awareness of the scope and the practicalities needed to realize the capstone may not be approved. For students who do not intend to complete a Capstone project, they must complete an additional two Advanced level courses. Students who successfully apply to do a Capstone project will have to complete Capstone I and II in their fourth year. The primary objective of Economics Major Capstone I is for students to produce a body of original economic research using theory and/or data. The project generally takes the form of an undergraduate thesis; however, students may design a non-traditional project with a substantial written component (e.g., a business proposal). Capstone projects should reflect student expertise in tools developed from Analysis courses in microeconomics, macroeconomics, and/or econometrics and often will apply economic analysis to problems in other disciplines.

### Question 37: Is it possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics? If yes, please provide a sample study plan.  
### Answer: 

It is possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics. However, the provided text does not give specific information on how to structure a double major program or provide a sample study plan. Therefore, while it is theoretically possible, the exact details of the study plan would depend on the specific requirements set by Fulbright University Vietnam and the guidelines for double majoring. For a precise study plan, consultation with an academic advisor is recommended.

### Question 40: What actions are considered plagiarism? Are AI-generated works counted?  
### Answer: 

Presenting text, images, or other content created by others or by generative AI as your own work, even at the sentence level, is considered plagiarism and grounds for failure of Capstone I and/or Capstone II. Therefore, AI-generated works are indeed counted and must be properly documented if used in the project.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]
Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout the project. This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, oﬀers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. 1.8. Grading process All Capstones are graded by the primary and secondary advisor, using what is known as a double-marking process. 1.9. ### Question 41: Why is the graduation requirement 128 credits, but the major requirement is only 48 credits?  
### Answer: 

The graduation requirement is 128 credits because it includes all the courses needed to fulfill general education, electives, and other non-major specific requirements. The major requirement is only 56 credits because it focuses solely on the courses directly related to the Computer Science major. Therefore, the major requirement is a subset of the overall graduation requirement.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. ### Question 42: Explain the cross-listed mechanism between courses.  
### Answer: 

The cross-listed mechanism allows students to use up to 8 credits (two courses) from one major to satisfy the requirements of another major or minor. This limit applies to each pair of majors or a major and a minor. However, this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For example, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. Therefore, the cross-listed mechanism provides flexibility for students to fulfill their requirements across different majors and minors, but it is subject to specific conditions and limitations.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. ### Question 44: How does the core quest course selection work to fulfill core credits?  
### Answer: 

To fulfill the core course credits, students need to complete five specific core courses, each worth 4 credits. The courses are: Global Humanities, Modern Vietnamese Culture and Society, Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age, Scientific Inquiry, and Design and Systems Thinking. Together, these courses amount to 20 credits, which is the total requirement for the core courses. There is no mention of selecting courses from different categories or fulfilling multiple categories with a single course. Each course is standalone and contributes equally to the core credit requirement.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
Class of 2027 students and earlier need to complete five core courses (20 credits). These core courses are: • Global Humanities (4 credits) • Modern Vietnamese Culture and Society (4 credits) • Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age (4 credits) • Scientific Inquiry (4 credits) • Design and Systems Thinking (4 credits). 13.2  Exploratory Requirements Exploratory requirements encourage students to step out of their comfort zone by exploring broad areas of study and discover more fully where their interests and passions lie. Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major.

### Question 45: Can I take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement. The context specifies that students are required to take six 200-level intermediate courses for their foundation courses, and these should ideally align with the specified sample courses for social/developmental psychology and counseling psychology. Taking a 300-level advanced course would not meet this requirement as it is meant for a different level of study and content depth. Therefore, a 300-level course cannot be used to fulfill a 200-level major requirement.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 69]

### Question 46: If I take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn’t have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, can I count it toward that major?  
### Answer: 

If you take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn't have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, you might still be able to count it toward that major. However, this depends on the specific policies and procedures of Fulbright regarding credit transfer and equivalency.

To ensure that the course can be counted towards your major at Fulbright, you would need to follow the process for applying for Credit Transfer. This involves submitting an Application for Credit Transfer, along with detailed information about the course, such as its curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. The Office of the Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether the credit can be transferred and applied to your major.

It's important to note that there are limitations on the amount of credit that can be transferred (a maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree). Additionally, the course must meet Fulbright's standards for equivalence to a course at Fulbright. Therefore, while it is possible that the course could be counted towards your major, it is not guaranteed without going through the official application and evaluation process.

### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you need a minimum of 128 credit hours to graduate from Fulbright. You currently have 128 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL, which totals 144 credits. Therefore, yes, you can graduate. However, it's important to ensure that these credits meet the specific requirements for your major and any other applicable requirements such as electives, capstones, etc. It's advisable to consult with an academic advisor to confirm that all requirements are met.

### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you cannot take only 2 courses in a regular semester if you want to maintain full-time enrollment status. Full-time enrollment typically requires registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. Taking only 2 courses would result in fewer than 12 academic credits, which does not meet the full-time enrollment requirement.

Regarding tuition fees, there is no mention of a reduction in tuition for students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, your tuition fees would not be reduced if you were to take only 2 courses. However, it's important to note that taking fewer than 12 credits might affect your financial aid eligibility. 

If you are facing circumstances where you need to take fewer courses, you should consult the Academic Advisor or the Dean’s Office to explore options such as requesting permission to reduce the number of courses for the term. They may require supporting documentation and authorization from relevant parties. Keep in mind that even with such authorization, no reduction in tuition is granted for fewer than 12 academic credits. 

In summary, you cannot take only 2 courses in a regular semester while maintaining full-time enrollment status, and your tuition fees would not be reduced for taking fewer than 12 credits. You should seek approval from the Academic Advisor or Dean’s Office if you need to take fewer courses due to specific circumstances.

### Answer:

It only discusses double majors and the rules related to them, such as completing all requirements for each major and the double-counting of up to 8 credits between pairs of majors or a major and a minor. There is no information given about pursuing three majors. Therefore, based on the given information, it is not possible to pursue 3 majors.

major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. ### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you need to follow the specific procedures outlined for each major. For example, for the Engineering major, you must complete the core course Design and Systems Thinking, one Mathematics or Basic Science course, and one Engineering course. For the Social Studies major, you need to complete Social Inquiry and at least two courses at the 100 or 200 level. For the Computer Science major, you need to complete at least two Computer Science courses, including MATH 202 - Discrete Math. Each major may have additional policies and requirements, so it's important to check the specific requirements for the major you wish to switch to. If there are any exceptions, they must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office. Additionally, you may need to coordinate with a supervisor for approval. It's recommended to consult with an academic advisor for guidance on the process. There is no mention of a specific acknowledgment page or thesis submission format in relation to changing your major declaration.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

The process of requesting a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment involves contacting Student Financial Services. They will first try to understand your circumstances and ask for a prompt response from you. During this period, you won't be able to register for new courses, attend classes, or participate in a Work-Study Program. You should meet with the Student Financial Services team early if you foresee difficulties in clearing the balance on time to seek assistance and alternative solutions. If you don't respond within the approved period, you might be placed on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for up to one term. After that, you could be withdrawn from Fulbright unless you confirm your intention to return by registering for courses or receive a leave extension approved by the Registrar's Office and Dean's Office. It's important to act promptly to avoid being placed on Admin LOA.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 54: Which major has the fewest requirements?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, the major with the fewest requirements appears to be the Engineering minor. It requires completing core course Design and Systems Thinking and one Engineering course. This is fewer requirements compared to the other majors mentioned like Computer Science, Economics, and Literature. Without the full details of all majors, we can only compare what is given here. Therefore, between the Engineering minor and Computer Science major, both have fewer requirements than the other majors mentioned.

### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 128 credits. However, physical education and political courses do not count towards this requirement. The exact number of courses will depend on the credit value of each course. Typically, a 3-credit course would mean taking about 43 courses (128/3), but this is just an approximation as courses can have different credit values. It's important to note that some courses can be double-counted towards different requirements, but this still needs to fit within the overall 128-credit requirement. Also, until the university can offer a robust list of 200 and 300-Level Courses, students can satisfy the 48 Credits with any combination of 200 and 300 Level Courses, as long as they meet the important note guidelines.

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 56: How many courses in a semester can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 20 credit hours per term according to the information provided in the document. However, this maximum course load requires completing a specific form and obtaining approval from your Academic Advisor. It's important to note that not all courses contribute towards the 128-credit requirement, such as Physical Education and Political courses. If you're facing initial academic difficulties, you might be advised to start with fewer courses and increase your course load as you become more comfortable with the academic demands. Always consult with your Academic Advisor to determine the appropriate course load for you.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

If you're going for a double major, the maximum number of courses that can be double-counted is 8 credits (two courses) per pair of majors. This means that for each combination of two majors, you can double-count up to 8 credits. However, this limit applies to each pair of majors separately, so if you have more than two majors, the total number of double-counted credits across all pairs could exceed 8 credits. For example, if you major in both A and B and minor in C, you could potentially have 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade translation from alphabetic to numerical at Fulbright University is as follows:
- 'A' corresponds to 4.0 grade points
- 'B+' corresponds to 3.7 grade points
- 'B' corresponds to 3.0 grade points
- 'B-' corresponds to 2.7 grade points
- 'C+' corresponds to 2.3 grade points
- 'C' corresponds to 2.0 grade points
- 'C-' corresponds to 1.7 grade points
- 'D+' corresponds to 1.3 grade points
- 'D' corresponds to 1.0 grade points
- 'D-' corresponds to 0.7 grade points
- 'F' corresponds to 0.0 grade points

Note: This grading scale is standard unless otherwise specified by the faculty for individual courses. The 'P' (Pass) and 'NP' (No Pass) grades are not included in the GPA calculation and do not have corresponding grade points. The 'I' (Incomplete) grade is temporary and is converted to a letter grade (including possibly 'F') if not resolved within the given timeframe. The 'W' (Withdrawal) grade is also not included in the GPA calculation.

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The process typically involves meeting with the Dean’s Office, who sets the conditions for your return to Fulbright. During the suspension period, which usually lasts one term or one academic year, you are not allowed to visit the Fulbright campus without specific permission from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for relevant meetings. You can be suspended a maximum of two times; if suspended a third time, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, and you will need to apply for re-admission, providing a letter explaining the reasons for your suspension and the steps you've taken to address those issues. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with faculty and staff.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade system operates under specific rules and conditions outlined in the provided context. Here's how it works:

1. **Eligibility**: Students can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) per academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis.

2. **Petition Process**: Students must submit a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday of Week 4 of the term (for a 16-week term).

3. **Conversion**: The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the final grade submitted by the instructor at the end of the term into either a Pass (P) or No Pass (NP) grade.

4. **Grading Criteria**:
   - A grade of 'C-' or higher is considered a Pass.
   - Any grade below a 'C-' is considered a No Pass (NP).
   - Courses with a NP grade do not grant any credit and cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

5. **Core Courses**: Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

6. **Irreversible Decision**: Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back.

7. **Incomplete Grades**: If a student is unable to complete the course due to exceptional circumstances, they might receive an incomplete grade ('I') instead. This incomplete grade needs to be resolved within 6 months; otherwise, it defaults to a No Pass (NP).

8. **Credit Requirement**: The system allows students to take up to 8 credits per academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis, but these credits do not contribute to core course requirements or major/minor requirements.

In summary, the P/NP grade system provides flexibility for students to manage their academic load, but it comes with strict guidelines regarding eligibility, conversion criteria, and the implications of choosing this grading option. It also emphasizes the importance of consulting with instructors and advisors before making the decision to petition for P/NP grades.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses as P/NP at once, and these courses will not be included in the official transcript GPA calculation. They will be shown on the Official Transcript with a 'NP' grade if you receive a grade below a 'C-'. Grades above 'C-' will be counted as a pass but will also not affect the GPA.

Without further details on the institution's rules, it cannot be definitively stated whether the failure will count toward the maximum credits. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. Exceptions will only be permitted in exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. In the case of approved exceptional circumstances, tuition credit will be considered and follow the “Fees & Charges Guide” for undergraduate students. No reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits.  Students should be aware that course withdrawals may  

</details> 

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

To receive an Academic Warning, students who are not making satisfactory progress towards their degree and/or fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity, will typically receive an Academic Warning. This is usually the first level of intervention. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. Three official warnings shall result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, here are some course suggestions to major in Math:

1. **Intermediate Courses (200 level)**:
   - Probability
   - Differential Equations
   - Discrete Mathematics
   - Numerical Analysis

2. **Advanced Courses (300 level)**:
   - Advanced Statistics
   - Statistical Learning
   - Stochastic Calculus
   - Numerical Analysis
   - Optimization
   - Partial Differential Equations

3. **Elective Applied Courses**:
   - Game Theory
   - The Economics of Corruption
   - Money and Banking
   - Economics of Inequality
   - Economics of Education
   - Cost-Benefit Analysis
   - Market Design
   - Signal, Systems, and Control
   - Computer Vision
   - Introduction to Machine Learning
   - Algorithm
   - Introduction to AI
   - Operations Research
   - Introduction to Quantitative Finance

4. **Pure Mathematics Courses**:
   - Abstract Algebra
   - Real Analysis

5. **Research Seminars**:
   - These provide opportunities to understand faculty's research and recent developments in mathematical research.

6. **Capstone Project (Optional)**:
   - A one-year long research project leading to a research paper or a product contributing to the knowledge of mathematics or its applications.

Remember, it's important to consult with an academic advisor to ensure the courses align with your specific goals and the requirements of your chosen program. Also, note that some courses might have prerequisites, so make sure to check those before enrolling. Additionally, avoid double counting courses for different requirements. For instance, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced or 1 Elective course. 

Good luck with your studies!

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses (MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted). This requirement ensures that students have a foundational understanding of key concepts in computer science before officially declaring the major. Completing these courses demonstrates the student's commitment and readiness to engage in the rigorous academic program required for the Computer Science major. Additionally, students should review the specific course offerings and prerequisites to ensure they meet all necessary criteria for declaring the major. Once the required courses are completed, students can proceed to formally declare their major through the appropriate academic advising office. It's important to note that meeting this requirement does not guarantee acceptance into the major, but it is a crucial step in the process. After declaration, students will be expected to continue fulfilling the major requirements outlined in the program description.

### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

To make a Capstone for graduation in the Computer Science major, follow these steps:

1. Understand the Capstone requirement: The capstone is a culmination of the student's curriculum, demonstrating the principal learning outcomes and competencies of the curriculum in a meaningful and coherent way.

2. Choose an appropriate topic: Select a topic that demonstrates original critical and creative thinking. Encourage primary research and consider the scope and practicalities needed to realize the capstone. Projects without current faculty expertise may not be approved.

3. Consult with your potential advisor: Early consultation with your potential advisor is essential to ensure a good match.

4. Develop a proposal: Think carefully about the appropriate scope of research and production for your proposed capstone.

5. Approval process: Applications which do not demonstrate awareness of the scope and the practicalities needed to realize the capstone may not be approved.

6. Grading process: The capstone is graded by a committee including all full-time faculty members. The primary advisor gives 60% of the grade, while the other committee members give 40%. 

7. Submission: Once approved, submit your capstone according to the guidelines provided. 

Remember, the capstone should be an individual project and can take only the form of a written thesis. It is important to keep in mind the guidelines and expectations set by the university-wide policy. Good luck!

### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

The information provided does not specify what grades are required to receive a distinctive graduation. The context discusses the grading process for capstones and general grading policies at Fulbright, but it does not mention any criteria for distinctive graduation. Therefore, the references are irrelevant to the question.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
The final grade for the thesis is the average of the 2 graders. The oral defense is graded by a panel of all IS faculty. See Appendix 1and 2 for detail rubrics on both the thesis and presentation. The total grade of the capstone is the sum of the thesis grade and oral defense grade. The primary advisor will communicate this result and any feedback from the graders to the student in writing. If there are any concerns about the grades, students should first meet with their primary advisor to discuss and clarify. If no agreement is made, the student could request one more grader (an IS faculty) to grade their submission, but cannot choose who the grader would be. The major coordinator will decide the 3rd grader after discussion with IS faculty team. The new grade would be the average of the 3 graders. Any further appeal after this would need to follow official UG program’s process for grade appeal.

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
GRADING: At Fulbright, the majority of courses apply a standard letter grade ranging from ‘A’ to ‘F.’ Grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale (unless otherwise decided by faculty in individual courses): Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 2]

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity. 1.10. Grading process Capstone I grade is decided by the primary advisor on pass/no pass basis. As for capstone II, there are two graders for each written thesis: • One grader must be the primary advisor • If there is a secondary advisor, they would be the other grader. Under circumstances in which the secondary advisor cannot grade the thesis, another IS faculty member will be assigned. • If there is not a secondary advisor, another IS faculty would be the second grader. The final grade for the thesis is the average of the 2 graders. The oral defense is graded by a panel of all IS faculty. See Appendix 1and 2 for detail rubrics on both the thesis and presentation. The total grade of the capstone is the sum of the thesis grade and oral defense grade. The primary advisor will communicate this result and any feedback from the graders to the student in writing. If there are any concerns about the grades, students should first meet with their primary advisor to discuss and

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
awarded a letter grade, which may be an ‘F’, based upon the work completed by the deadline. The student must fill out an Incomplete Grade Request form. A ‘W’ does not affect the student’s GPA. • Grade Point Average (GPA): GPA is calculated by dividing [the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course] by [the total attempted credits for GPA]. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. • Grade Reports (Transcript): At the end of each term, grade reports are available for viewing on the Fulbright One Stop portal, named Unofficial Transcript. ### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honor or lie within the top GPA, you need to maintain a minimum GPA threshold of 3.5/4 by the summer of your third year. This involves excelling in your courses, particularly in Capstone I and Capstone II, which are 4-credit courses. Additionally, you should adhere to the university's core and exploratory requirements, which may undergo revisions communicated to all Sociology majors by the latest during the second semester of their third year. Excelling in these areas and receiving an Honors Pass on Capstone II can significantly contribute to achieving a high GPA. Remember to consult with your Academic/Major Advisor to ensure you're on track for honors.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 2 courses with a Pass/No Pass grade in one academic year. This is based on the information provided in the context, which states that "take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis". Therefore, you can take 2 courses with a Pass/No Pass grade in total during one academic year.

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. ### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are two main types of absences mentioned in the given text: excused and unexcused absences. However, the text also discusses specific categories of leave of absence which can be considered as subtypes of excused absences. These include personal leave, medical leave, administrative leave of absence, and leave due to participation in a sponsored academic event or exceptional circumstances. Therefore, there are at least four types of absences discussed in the text.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. You can have a leave of absence by meeting the criteria for one of these types, such as having a personal reason, a medical condition, or an outstanding student account balance without requesting a late or extension of tuition fee payment. The duration is determined in conjunction with relevant offices and a health services professional. Indefinite leaves are not permitted. For an Administrative Leave of Absence, you must also meet specific financial criteria and allow the Student Financial Services team to determine your circumstances. Before being placed on this type of leave, they will request a timely response from you.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity. If a case of academic dishonesty is reported, the Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office. An investigation follows, during which, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. However, if mediation is not possible, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office to conduct an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation becomes the final grade. For cases involving the interpretation of course policies, the Dean’s Office defers to the course syllabus whenever possible; otherwise, they make a final ruling. This policy is effective from the date of signing and is reviewed annually for the upcoming academic year. Any significant changes require approval by the Dean’s Office and the Provost before being published and made available in the One Stop portal. The handling process ensures fairness and consistency in addressing academic integrity issues.
