### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

The policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades are outlined as follows:

1. For core courses, students must repeat the course if they receive a grade of 'F'. For courses that count toward a major or minor, students must repeat the course if they receive a grade below 'C-'.

2. Students may also retake a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP' for the course, or if they have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'.

3. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with the student's academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. This consideration includes course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year.

4. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript.

5. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits.

6. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet major requirements.

7. Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.

These policies aim to provide students with opportunities to improve their grades while maintaining academic integrity and ensuring that the GPA calculation reflects the highest achieved grade.

APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the  

</details> 

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance by considering these as exceptional circumstances. These circumstances include exceptional medical conditions such as hospitalization or incapacitation due to injury, illness, or mental health crises. The university also considers close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and unforeseeable transport difficulties as examples of exceptional circumstances. Students experiencing these situations are expected to provide appropriate documentation and contact their instructors to arrange for making up any missed work. The instructors are responsible for allowing the students to make up missed assignments if the absence is reasonable and informing the students if they are in danger of failing the course due to class absence or missed assignments. The university encourages instructors to outline the expectations regarding students' attendance at the beginning of each term and to communicate the likely consequences of any class absence without permission. Additionally, the university may pursue a course withdrawal or an Incomplete grade if appropriate under the University policies. Students are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. For university-sponsored events, the faculty or supervising staff responsible for the event requests a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form and submits it to the Dean's Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar's Office informed. Students must be in good academic standing and not on probation to be excused from the class. The faculty or supervising staff is responsible for checking the student's academic standing with the Registrar's Office before approving the excused absence form. Emergency cases are also considered, where students must be absent from class due to an emergency situation but are unable to communicate their condition to the instructor(s).  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but under specific conditions. According to the provided context, any creative projects involving generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should clearly define the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to. Additionally, students need to specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed, outline how AI will be incorporated, and address ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI. This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, offers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. Therefore, while students can use AI tools like ChatGPT, they must follow these guidelines to ensure academic integrity and proper documentation.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

You can get support for mental health treatment through various resources mentioned in the context, such as the Mental Health First Aid Training Program, Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes, Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, and Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program. These initiatives aim to address mental health needs within the community and provide guidance and support for those seeking mental health treatment. However, it's important to note that these programs are part of a broader educational and awareness-raising effort rather than direct clinical services. For direct mental health treatment, you should consult local mental health service providers or healthcare professionals.

Fulbright is committed to supporting student learning when absences are unavoidable.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit of studied courses from another university towards your Fulbright undergraduate degree, you should follow these steps:

1. Gather all the necessary information about the courses you want to transfer, such as the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

2. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer to the Office of the Registrar at Fulbright University Vietnam.

3. Include the required information on the course(s) in the application.

4. Await coordination between the Office of the Registrar and the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

5. If your application is successful, the approved courses will be recorded on your Official Transcript under the "Transfer Credit" section in the following term. 

Remember, a maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. Ensure that you meet this requirement to earn your Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Answer:

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided in the context, it seems that you are no longer living in the university dormitory as you moved out after your first year. However, the context does not provide specific details about the university's policy regarding re-registration for dormitory accommodation or financial support for third-year students who wish to move into dormitories.

To answer your questions:
1. Whether you can register again for dormitory accommodation: This would depend on the university's policies and availability of dormitory spaces. Since you are a third-year student, you might need to check with the Residential Life office to see if there are any available spots and if you meet the eligibility criteria.
2. Whether you will still have financial support: Financial support for dormitory accommodation typically depends on the university's financial aid policies and your current financial situation. You should consult with the Office of the Registrar and the Financial Aid Office to determine your eligibility for financial assistance.

In summary, you should contact the Residential Life office and the Financial Aid Office to inquire about your options for re-registering for dormitory accommodation and to discuss your financial support needs. They will be able to provide you with more specific information based on your individual circumstances.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are three ways provided by the university for students to get support in their academic path:

1. Access to labs, tools, and software relevant to their project work.
2. Support for learning new software or techniques where necessary.
3. Mentorship and Industry Involvement, including industry mentors who may provide project guidance, act as secondary advisors for Capstone projects, and participate in grading as either secondary advisors or members of the capstone panel. 

These three methods aim to assist students in their academic journey and project work.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided in the context, you should follow these steps:

1. Discuss the matter with the course instructor(s) first to resolve the issue. This is the first step in addressing your concerns.

2. If the matter remains unresolved and you believe there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, you may file an appeal.

3. To file an appeal, submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term.

4. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean’s Office of the case. 

5. If the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. However, if mediation is not successful, the Registrar's Office will organize a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade.

6. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade.

7. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

By following these steps, you can escalate your concerns to higher authorities and seek a resolution to the issue you're facing with the professor's teaching methods.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 2]

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
• The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and

### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

For your request regarding obtaining an official transcript and seeking absence approval for attending a tournament with the Fulbright Basketball Club, you should contact the Office of the Registrar and your course instructors respectively.

For the official transcript:
- Contact the Office of the Registrar to request your official transcript.

For seeking absence approval:
- Discuss your absence directly with your course instructors. They can provide you with the necessary forms and guidance on how to handle your absence for the tournament. 

Additionally, since you are a member of the Fulbright Basketball Club, you might want to inform the club advisor or coach about your plans, as they could also provide support and ensure that your absence is handled appropriately within the club context. However, the primary responsibility for obtaining the official transcript and seeking approval for class absences lies with you and your instructors.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively on a major report, follow these steps:

1. **Executive Summary**: Start by creating an executive summary that outlines the problem, purpose, current state, proposed solution, evaluation findings, and their implications. Ensure this section is well-structured and concise, adhering to the 200-250 word limit.

2. **Formatting and Referencing**: Review and correct the formatting and referencing of your entire evaluation report. This includes ensuring each chapter starts on a new page, verifying chapter numbering and the Table of Contents, aligning in-text citations and the Reference List, and including all required Appendices such as documentation.

3. **Finalization**: Convert the Word file into a single PDF document after making all necessary revisions. This ensures the report is ready for submission.

4. **Additional Deliverables**: Prepare additional materials like presentation slides, demonstration videos, and any other supplementary information as specified in the submission requirements.

5. **Presentation and Q&A**: Be prepared for up to 10 minutes of Q&A with the judging panel and audience following your presentation.

6. **Project Objectives, Methods, and Findings**: Articulate and justify the project's objectives, methods, and findings through written, visual, and oral communication. This should map to the relevant major learning outcomes and course learning objectives (CLOs).

7. **Capstone Report**: For a capstone report, ensure it is a production book that includes all pre-production deliverables and production documents. This should cover legal releases, call sheets, test audiences, and marketing and distribution plans. The word count should not exceed 5000 words excluding production documents.

By following these steps, you can ensure that your major report is comprehensive, well-structured, and meets all the specified requirements.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: HCE_Capstone_Handbook_Final_2025.01.16.pdf, Page: 5]

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fill in the requirements of the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) by completing at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits. Experiential Learning can also count toward elective or major requirements with advisor approval. This means you have flexibility in how you meet these requirements, depending on your academic plan and advisor's input.
